10 min
Mahr and Iddah After Remarriage During Iddah and Subsequent Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr and iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad's opposing view on mahr and iddah in the case of remarriage during iddah and divorce before consummation, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Prior consummation carries over to the new marriage, triggering full mahr and new iddah.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a specific scenario: a man divorces his wife irrevocably (bain), then remarries her during her iddah, and divorces her again before consummation. The question is whether she receives full or half mahr, and whether she must observe a new iddah or complete the first one. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply istihsan and qiyas within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
A man divorces his wife with a bain divorce (irrevocable). During her iddah, he remarries her (permissible since she is still in iddah for him). Then before consummation of the second marriage, he divorces her again.
The bain divorce severs marital ties but the woman is still in iddah for the same husband.
2
Identify the issue
Two issues arise: what mahr is due (full or half) and what iddah must she observe (a new complete iddah or finish the first).
3
Study the majority position (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf)
They rule full mahr and a new full iddah. Their proof: the previous consummation is considered as consummation in the second marriage (istihsan), because the iddah is a continuous period.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Study Imam Muhammad's opposing view
Imam Muhammad rules half mahr and completion of the first iddah. His proof: no new consummation occurred, so apply the general rule (qiyas) that divorce before consummation gives half mahr and no separate iddah.
He does not consider the first consummation as carrying over.
5
Contrast the proofs and determine the tarjih
The majority uses istihsan (juristic preference) based on the continuity of iddah, while Imam Muhammad uses strict qiyas. The Hanafi school gives weight to the majority view as the relied-upon position.
Remember the principle: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' does not directly apply here; rather it's about the effect of a continuous iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۱۱] (۳۳) اگر آدمی نے اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائنہ دی۔ پھر اس کی عدت ہی میں اس سے شادی کی اور اس سے صحبت سے پہلے اس کو طلاق دی تو شوہر پر پورا مہر ہے اور عورت پر اگلی عدت ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا عورت کے لئے آدھا مہر ہے اور اس پر پہلی عدت کو پورا کرنا ہے۔ ... تو امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شوہر پر پورا مہر لازم ہوگا ۔ اور اس طلاق کی مستقل عدت گزارنی ہوگی۔ اگر چہ اس نکاح میں صحبت نہیں کی ہے اس لئے عدت لازم نہیں ہونی چاہئے اور مہر بھی آدھا لازم ہونا چاہئے لیکن یہاں، مہر بھی پورا لازم ہو گا اور مستقل طور پر پوری عدت بھی گزارنی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ پہلے نکاح میں جو صحبت ہوئی ہے وہی اس نکاح میں بھی گن لی جائے گی تو گویا کہ اس نکاح میں بھی صحبت کر لی اس لئے مہر بھی پورا لا زم ہوگا اور عدت بھی پوری لازم ہوگی ... اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ عورت کو آدھا مہر ملے گا اور مستقل عدت لازم نہیں ہوگی بلکہ پہلی عدت جو باقی رہ گئی ہے اسی کو پوری کرے۔ چونکہ دوسری شادی میں صحبت نہیں کی ہے اس لئے مہر بھی آدھا لا زم ہوگا اور مستقل طور پر عدت بھی لازم نہیں ہوگی۔
If a man gives his wife an irrevocable divorce, then marries her during her iddah, and then divorces her before consummation, then the husband must pay the full mahr and the woman must observe a new iddah. Imam Muhammad said: The woman gets half the mahr and she must complete the first iddah. ... According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, the full mahr is obligatory and a new full iddah must be observed. Even though there was no consummation in this marriage, so iddah should not be required and mahr should be half, but here full mahr and full iddah are required because the previous consummation is counted as consummation in this marriage as well. ... Imam Muhammad said: The woman gets half the mahr and a new iddah is not required; rather she completes the remaining part of the first iddah.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf on one side, and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the other, regarding a specific scenario: A man gives his wife an irrevocable divorce (talq bain), then during her iddah he marries her again (which is permissible since she is in iddah for him), and then divorces her before consummation. The question is: what mahr is due and what iddah must she observe? Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that the full mahr is due and she must observe a new, complete iddah (three menstrual cycles or three months). Their reasoning is that the previous consummation from the first marriage is considered as if it occurred in the second marriage, since the iddah is continuous. Thus, she is considered as having been consummated with, triggering full mahr and a new iddah. Imam Muhammad disagrees: since there was no new consummation, she only gets half the mahr (as per the rule for divorce before consummation in a new marriage), and she must complete the remainder of her first iddah, not start a new one. Both sides cite athars from early authorities. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as the text implies by presenting it as the primary ruling.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talāq bā'in): An irrevocable divorce (third divorce or divorce before consummation) that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot return without a new marriage and consummation.
عدۃ (ʿiddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference – departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable result based on a stronger evidence.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction – extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what iddah must a woman observe if she is divorced before consummation after being remarried during her iddah?
A) She completes the remainder of her first iddah.
B) She observes a new full iddah.
C) No iddah is required.
D) She observes iddah of one month.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if a woman is remarried during her iddah and then divorced before consummation, the preferred view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) holds that full mahr and a new complete iddah are due, based on istihsan.

Lineage of a Child Born to a Revocably Divorced Wife
Ruling on establishing paternity of a child born to a revocably divorced woman within two years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the lineage of a child born to a revocably divorced wife, identify the conditions for its application, and apply the hadith 'al-waladu lil-firash' to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
A revocably divorced woman's child is attributed to the husband if born within two years, as long as she does not admit the iddah ended.

This passage addresses the question of paternity when a woman is revocably divorced and later gives birth. In Hanafi law, the revocably divorced wife remains in the husband's 'firash' (marital bed) during the iddah period, which can be extended due to pregnancy. The ruling is grounded in the prophetic hadith 'the child belongs to the bed.' This lesson unpacks the conditions and proof for establishing lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the birth of a child to a revocably divorced woman. The ruling is that the child's lineage (nasab) is established to the husband if she gives birth within two years of the divorce, provided she has not admitted that her iddah has ended.
The two-year period is the maximum length of pregnancy according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the prophetic hadith 'al-waladu lil-firash' (the child belongs to the bed), which is transmitted by Bukhari and Muslim.
The hadith is considered mutawatir in meaning and qat'i in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'lil-firash' implies that the child is attributed to the husband of the woman who is in his 'firash'. The revocably divorced woman remains in the husband's firash during her iddah because the marriage is not fully dissolved. Therefore, the child born during this period is legally his.
The link is that 'firash' here does not require physical presence; it is a legal status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) limit the maximum iddah period to a shorter duration (e.g., nine months or one year). The Hanafi school maintains two years based on reported cases of prolonged pregnancy.
The practical difference is the timeframe within which lineage is established.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that the two-year period is supported by the generality of the hadith and by istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve lineage wherever possible. The wife's admission of iddah ending is taken as decisive because it is her own testimony against her claim.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۱۱۲] (۳۴) ويثبت نسب ولد المطلقة الرجعية اذا جائت به لسنتين او اکثر مالم تقر بانقضاء عدتها. ... ثابت ہو گا مطلقہ رجعیہ کے بچے کا نسب جب وہ جنے دو سال یا زیادہ میں جب تک کہ وہ عدت گزرنے کا اقرار نہ کرے۔ بیوی کو طلاق رجعی دی۔ وہ عدت گزار رہی تھی ، دو سال یا اس سے زیادہ تک عدت گزرنے کا اقرار نہیں کیا۔ اس درمیان اس نے بچہ دیا تو اس بچے کا نسب باپ سے ثابت ہوگا۔ جب تک عدت گزرنے کا اقرار نہ کرے اس وقت تک وہ شوہر کی فراش ہے، اور جب وہ فراش ہے تو بچہ اسی کا ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے که بچہ فراش والے کا ہوتا ہے۔ ...
And the lineage of the child of a revocably divorced woman is established if she gives birth within two years or more, as long as she does not admit to the expiration of her iddah. ... The lineage of the revocably divorced woman's child will be established when she gives birth within two years or more, as long as she does not confess that her iddah has ended. The wife was given a revocable divorce; she was observing her iddah, and she did not confess that her iddah ended for two years or more. If she gave birth in between, the child's lineage is established to the father. As long as she does not confess that the iddah ended, she remains in the husband's bed (firash), and when she is in his bed, the child belongs to him. The hadith states: 'The child belongs to the bed.'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the lineage (nasab) of a child born to a revocably divorced woman. The ruling: the child's lineage is established to the husband if the woman gives birth within two years (or more) of the divorce, provided she has not explicitly stated that her iddah has ended. The reasoning is that the woman remains in the husband's 'firash' (marital bed) as long as the iddah is not confirmed to have expired. Since the iddah could be prolonged due to pregnancy (the longest possibility in Hanafi fiqh being two years), any child born within that period is attributed to the husband. The proof is the famous hadith: 'al-waladu lil-firash' (the child belongs to the bed). The author also notes that if the woman admits the iddah has ended, the ruling changes. This ruling emphasizes the Hanafi school's approach of preserving lineage wherever possible.

Key Terms
فراش (firāsh): Marital bed; metaphorically, the state of being in a valid marriage or revocable divorce iddah such that the husband is entitled to intimacy and the woman is considered under his protection.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity, the legal attribution of a child to its father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman is given a revocable divorce. She does not admit that her iddah has ended and gives birth after 18 months. What is the ruling on the child's lineage?
A) The child's lineage is not established to the husband.
B) The child's lineage is established to the husband.
C) The child is considered illegitimate.
D) The child's lineage is established to the mother only.

Key Takeaway
A revocably divorced woman's child belongs to the husband if born within two years unless she admits iddah ends, based on the hadith 'al-waladu lil-firash'.
